    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1858461273" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1858461273" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1858461273?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=the-best-of-the-best">the-best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1858461273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13507917037161056692"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1858461273' rel='nofollow noopener'>Every Heart a Doorway</a> ★★★★★<br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1975724096' rel='nofollow noopener'>Down Among the Sticks and Bones</a> ★★★★★<br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2186219230' rel='nofollow noopener'>Beneath the Sugar Sky</a> ★★★★★<br/>#4 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2365854734' rel='nofollow noopener'>In An Absent Dream</a> ★★★★★<br/>#5 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2365854622' rel='nofollow noopener'>Come Tumbling Down</a> ★★★★★<br/>#6 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3313598944' rel='nofollow noopener'>Across the Green Grass Fields</a> ★★★★★</blockquote> <br/>I somehow lived a full 25 years of my life without experiencing Seanan McGuire’s writing, and now that I’ve seen how incredible her story-telling is, I can’t imagine ever letting it go. This book sucked me in so wholly in such a short number of pages – it made me laugh, cry, and my heart soared. I was so i</span>
  <span id="freeText13507917037161056692" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1858461273" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Heart a Doorway</a> ★★★★★<br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1975724096" rel="nofollow noopener">Down Among the Sticks and Bones</a> ★★★★★<br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2186219230" rel="nofollow noopener">Beneath the Sugar Sky</a> ★★★★★<br />#4 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2365854734" rel="nofollow noopener">In An Absent Dream</a> ★★★★★<br />#5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2365854622" rel="nofollow noopener">Come Tumbling Down</a> ★★★★★<br />#6 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3313598944" rel="nofollow noopener">Across the Green Grass Fields</a> ★★★★★</blockquote> <br />I somehow lived a full 25 years of my life without experiencing Seanan McGuire’s writing, and now that I’ve seen how incredible her story-telling is, I can’t imagine ever letting it go. This book sucked me in so wholly in such a short number of pages – it made me laugh, cry, and my heart soared. I was so invested in these characters, so fearful for them and desperately wishing I could protect them, that by the end of the story, I felt stunned. How could Seanan possibly do, in 173 pages, what so many authors fail to do in 600?<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> Eleanor West spent her days giving them what she had never had, and hoped that someday, it would be enough to pay her passage back to the place where she belonged.</i>
</blockquote><br />In a world where children stumble upon doorways leading to other worlds, sometimes, those children are sent back – and left without any way of coping with the “real world” that they’re expected to mold seamlessly into. They spend their lives suffering through parents and doctors insisting that everything was a dream or delusion, when all these children want is to find that door again, and to go back where they belong.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> She was a woman with something to protect. That made her more dangerous than they could ever have suspected.</i>
</blockquote><br />That’s where Eleanor West comes in: a woman who gave up her door, to give these children a safe place to continues their searches whilst living as peacefully as their minds will allow. She is fiercely protective and loving of her students, determined to offer them a home away from the worlds they so desperately wanted to return to. I loved her instantly.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“If anyone should be kind, understanding, accepting, loving to their fellow outcasts, it’s you. All of you. You are the guardians of the secrets of the universe, beloved of worlds that most will never dream of, much less see… can’t you see where you owe it to yourselves to be kind? To care for one another?”</i>
</blockquote><br />Of course, not all of these children are returned unscathed, and that’s where our murder mystery comes in. Students at the school keep turning up dead, corpses brutalized. Nancy is new to the school, but having been a child of the Underworld, death doesn’t scare her, and she finds herself joining in a small team of students determined to track down the murderer by any means necessary. Seanan’s writing is dark and heavy – gruesome, at most – but the suspense isn’t even the best part (though the mystery is, in fact, fantastic).<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“We notice the silence of men. We depend upon the silence of women.”</i>
</blockquote><br />At its core, this story and the characters within it are so inherently feminist and inclusive, and I love Seanan <i>so much</i> for that. Despite it being a fantasy tale, a tremendous amount of the advice given and commentary made was incredibly relevant to our own world and society.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> She’d known girls on diet her entire life. Most of them had been looking for smaller waists, clearer complexions, and richer boyfriends, spurred on by a deeply ingrained self-loathing that had been manufactured for them before they were old enough to understand the kind of quicksand they were sinking in.</i>
</blockquote><br />There’s not only a great deal of talk about toxic masculinity and how our culture accepts terrible crimes from men, simply because they are men, but there’s also commentary on the unfair standards women are scrutinized under. It felt incredibly important to me that one of the characters even points out that there are so few boys at the school, and is answered with an explanation that, as men are typically allowed to do as they please, they don’t suffer the same fine-toothed combing that a woman’s every move and word is passed under. When they go away to the other worlds, their disappearance is viewed as less of a shock, and when they come back changed, their newfound behaviors don’t deem them a <i>problem child</i> in the same ways.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> She could have flirted forever. It was just the things that came after flirting that she had no interest in.</i>
</blockquote><br />Of course, the feminism in the writing isn’t the only delightfully inclusive aspect to it; it’s also a book with wonderfully diverse representation throughout the cast, including both an asexual protagonist and a trans friend/love interest. Their sexual orientations and gender identities aren’t merely hinted at; they are displayed proudly on the page, which isn’t something we see often in fantasy novels, much less little novellas like this one. It was evident from the start that Seanan cares enough about representation to find room for it no matter how small the page count may be, and I appreciated that so much.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> This was always the difficult part, back when she’d been at her old school: explaining that “asexual” and “aromantic” were different things.</i>
</blockquote><br />Not only does she offer such wonderful rep, but she also takes the time to dismantle a few myths, tropes, and assumptions. We have an asexual character, explaining that ace does not equal aro, and that she’s capable of romantic interest and physical affections, regardless of her views on sex itself. I don’t think I’ve ever read a book with such prominent ace rep, and while I’m not on the ace spectrum myself, I thought that it came across as fantastically positive rep.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You’re nobody’s doorway but your own, and the only one who gets to tell you how your story ends is you.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I could honestly ramble forever about this little story, but the bottom line is that it is an incredible tale of acceptance, healing, friendship, trauma, and finding yourself – be it in this world, or another. I cannot recommend this series highly enough, and I am so eager to continue it and see what else Seanan has in store.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13507917037161056692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1602390420" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1602390420" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1602390420?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1602390420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9628999362980265640"><i>“You found freedom, if only for a moment, and when you lost it, you came here, hoping it could be found again.”</i><br/><br/>This story started out grand and sprawling, a majestic, epic tale of finding out what happens when you come back to an unwanted reality after living in a magical place.<br/>And yet somewhere along the way, it didn’t work for me.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454440815ra/17963249.gif' width='360' height='230' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>This book read more like a short story than a full novel and I liked that. But there were a lot of dull moments here and there, especially when tragedy struck. And I</span>
  <span id="freeText9628999362980265640" style="display:none"><i>“You found freedom, if only for a moment, and when you lost it, you came here, hoping it could be found again.”</i><br><br>This story started out grand and sprawling, a majestic, epic tale of finding out what happens when you come back to an unwanted reality after living in a magical place.<br>And yet somewhere along the way, it didn’t work for me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454440815ra/17963249.gif" width="360" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This book read more like a short story than a full novel and I liked that. But there were a lot of dull moments here and there, especially when tragedy struck. And I couldn’t really seem to care about any of it because I wasn’t attached to the world.<br><br>That’s not to say that the storyline isn’t incredibly intriguing, I just cared more about the stories of their journeys into the other world than what was going on in the aftermath of coming back. The stories they told in group therapy of finding <i>the door</i> and what happened when they went through it interested me so much.<br><br><i>“What about, like, Narnia?” asked Christopher. “Those kids went through all sorts of different doors, and they always wound up back with the big talking lion.”<br>“That’s because Narnia was a Christian allegory pretending to be a fantasy series, you asshole,” said one of the other boys. “C. S. Lewis never went through any doors. He didn’t know how it worked. He wanted to tell a story, and he’d probably heard about kids like us, and he made shit up. That’s what all those authors did. They made shit up, and people made them famous. We tell the truth, and our parents throw us into this glorified loony bin.”</i><br><br>What I missed from this novel was <b>something more</b>. <br>Halfway through the book I started to lose interest and I couldn’t understand why. There would be a chapter where I would feel fully invested in the story, only to turn to the next and get distracted by almost everything.<br>The premise of this story is so different and intriguing, yet the execution of it did not work in my favor.<br><br><b>2.5 stars</b><br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</i> <b>Every Heart a Doorway</b>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link. I'll make a small commission!*</i><br><a target="_blank" href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0765385503/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=0765385503&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=natalie013-20&amp;linkId=f207d6872f33f24fa6a46f93466665ca" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482935740i/21563581.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482935740i/21563582.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">This review and more can be found on my blog.</a></span>

<div id="review_2036623003" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2036623003" />
    <a title="Always Pouting" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting"><img alt="Always Pouting" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483476563p2/48650982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2036623003?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Always Pouting" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Always Pouting" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting">Always Pouting</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25533896-every-heart-a-doorway">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2036623003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10170397128658951861">Eleanor West's School for Wayward Children takes in kids who have trouble readjusting to life after being found again. These kid's stories of where they have been are fantastic and hard to believe, leading parents to worry, especially when many of the kids seem depressed to be back. Kids are taken to the school to undergo therapy to let go of their delusions of the time they spent away from home and deal with the emotional fallout, or so the parents think. Eleanor West may tell the parents what </span>
  <span id="freeText10170397128658951861" style="display:none">Eleanor West's School for Wayward Children takes in kids who have trouble readjusting to life after being found again. These kid's stories of where they have been are fantastic and hard to believe, leading parents to worry, especially when many of the kids seem depressed to be back. Kids are taken to the school to undergo therapy to let go of their delusions of the time they spent away from home and deal with the emotional fallout, or so the parents think. Eleanor West may tell the parents what they want to hear, but she knows that the children she takes in aren't lying and gives them a safe haven where they can talk about their experiences and meet other children like themselves. The school tries to help these children learn to navigate in the world now that they know about the other world that exists where they feel more at home, like they belong completely. Nancy is a new student at the school and soon after her arrival mysterious accidents being to occur. <br /><br />I enjoyed the book a lot actually and if I have any complaints its that I wish there was more of it. It was more of a novella than a book and I really wish there was more details about the other worlds because I found that really fascinating especially hearing about the other kids experiences, not just Nancy. I also liked the whole murder mystery but it felt sort of obvious as to who it was and I wish that we had at least had some time to become attached to the characters before they started dropping dead so I could've cared more that they were dead. I do like the autonomy extended to the characters and the diversity represented in the book though and I really enjoyed that the children were allowed to talk about and make peace with their experiences which is important for people to be allowed to do. The characters were interesting too, I especially liked Jack and Jill but for some reason I couldn't get into liking Kade as much but it might just be because he felt like he was being put into the YA role of the broody hot guy and it automatically made me feel like ugh. <br /><br />It's a creative idea and kudos for the diversity but again just wish there was more detail on the other worlds and maybe a better explanation of why there were more girls than boys because if anything I feel like parents tend to be more protective of their daughters and also does it matter how hard they search for a child if its in a different world we can't access. I just want more explanation for all of it and more detail about the other worlds and kids experiences.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10170397128658951861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1590255634?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fairytales">fairytales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=ace-character">ace-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1590255634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10012188761073016466"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465852916i/19408865._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>▐ <b>WINNER OF THE HUGO AWARDS 2017 for best novella</b>▐<br/><br/><i>As I hated them as a child, of course I had to write a review this way. That's my High Logic combating my High Nonsense for you. You're welcome.</i> <br/><br/><b>► <u>START HERE</u></b> : <b>Have you ever wished that you could escape this world and discover another one in which you would really belong?</b><br/>■ <b>YES :</b> Go to #1<br/>■ <b>NO :</b> Go to #8<br/><br/><b>#0</b> <i>"This world is unforgiving and cruel to those it judges as even the slightest bit outside the norm."</i> <b>Want more?</b> Go to #3<br/><br/><b>#1</b> First off, welcome! Y</span>
  <span id="freeText10012188761073016466" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465852916i/19408865._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>▐ <b>WINNER OF THE HUGO AWARDS 2017 for best novella</b>▐<br><br><i>As I hated them as a child, of course I had to write a review this way. That's my High Logic combating my High Nonsense for you. You're welcome.</i> <br><br><b>► <u>START HERE</u></b> : <b>Have you ever wished that you could escape this world and discover another one in which you would really belong?</b><br>■ <b>YES :</b> Go to #1<br>■ <b>NO :</b> Go to #8<br><br><b>#0</b> <i>"This world is unforgiving and cruel to those it judges as even the slightest bit outside the norm."</i> <b>Want more?</b> Go to #3<br><br><b>#1</b> First off, welcome! You're about to start a fantastic journey, full of adventures, friendships, betrayals, suspicions..... Okaaaay I'm overdoing it. When starting <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25526296.Every_Heart_a_Doorway__Wayward_Children___1_" title="Every Heart a Doorway (Wayward Children, #1) by Seanan McGuire" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Heart a Doorway</a>, you shouldn't expect an action-packed novel, because it couldn't be further from what you'll get. <br><br>► <b>Are you still interested in this perfect mix of creepy atmosphere and hilarious dark humor?</b><br>■ <b>YES :</b> Go to #2<br>■ <b>NO :</b> Go to #10<br><br><b>#2</b> Not to say that this novel was <i>plotless</i>, because an important part of the story revolved around a murder mystery, but in my opinion its strength lay elsewhere : in the issues dealt with, first of these being the way we humans need to satisfy our thirst for acceptance and understanding - for <i>hope</i>. <br><br>► <b>Now tell me, how would you describe your relationship with morally ambiguous characters?</b> <br>■ <b>I'd rather not say</b> : Go to #5<br>■ <b>Pretty good, actually</b> : Go to #4<br>■ <b>God, I hate them</b> : Go to #7<br><br><b>#3</b> Sometimes you find friendship in the most unexpected places, you know? Of course, of <i>course</i>, a boarding school shouldn't be so surprising a place, but given that 99% of the students want to run away <i>elsewhere</i> and suffer from some kind of PTSD, bonding with each other is often easier said than done. Yet Candy, Kade, Jack, Jill, Sumi and Christopher (Skeleton Boy! I would call dibs, but that would be Neanderthal<i>-ish</i>, wouldn't it? Sigh) delighted me with their interactions. <b>Fantastic characters' dynamics, really. <br><br>► Need more convincing? How about some quotes, okay?</b> <br>■ <i>"Because 'boys will be boys' is a self-fulfilling prophecy..."</i> Go to #6<br>■ <i>"This is not an asylum, and you are not mad - and so what if you were?..."</i> Go to #0<br>■ <i>"If they corner her because they've decided I'm guilty, she's liable to hurt someone just so she can get away..."</i> Go to #9<br>■ <i>"Time resumed..."</i> Go to #11<br><br><b>#4</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2860219.Seanan_McGuire" title="Seanan McGuire" rel="nofollow noopener">Seanan McGuire</a>'s characters aren't morally ambiguous, <b>they use different scales of values as reference</b>. And yes, by that I mean that each and every one of them offers a different definition for the old Goods and Evils. Their past in the fantastic world they discovered and the way their life unfolded once they returned "Home" - they <i>matter</i> : These characters are different, intriguing and fascinating. <br><br>► <b>Alright - Are you ready to meet the oddest group of friends?</b> <br>■ <b>YES</b> : Go to #3<br>■ <b>NO</b> : Go to #10<br><br><b>#5</b> BAHAHAHAHAHA REALLY, did you think you could get away with this? Go to #4<br><br><b>#6</b> <i>"Call it irony, if you like, but we spend so much time waiting for our boys to stray that they never have the opportunity. We notice the silence of men. We depend upon the silence of women."</i> <b>Want more?</b> Go to #3<br><br><b>#7</b> The funny thing is, this is not relevant. Go to #4<br><br><b>#8</b> : I don't know what to tell you, really. I mean, have you watched the news? Please go watch the news. <br>■ <b>If you changed your mind</b> : Go to #1<br>■ <b>If you didn't</b> : Go to #10<br><br><b>#9</b> <i>"I'd rather not get expelled right after I've disposed of a body. Seems like a waste of good acid."</i> <b>Want more?</b> Go to #3<br><br><b>#10</b> : Hey, no hard feelings, but GAME OVER. Try again? <br><br><b>#11</b> : <i>"Time had a way of doing that."</i> <b>Want more?</b> Go to #3<br><br>PS. Tell me, was it supposed to be hilarious? Because somehow I couldn't stop laughing? Or is it yet another case of, Anna, really, your sense of humor sucks big time? I guess we'll never know. <br><br>Hole : <a href="http://artsy-antics.deviantart.com/art/Hole-3-376534510" rel="nofollow noopener">credit</a><br>Old Book : <a href="http://vixen525.deviantart.com/art/Blank-Vintage-Book-362830364" rel="nofollow noopener">credit</a><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2597026490" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2597026490" />
    <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court"><img alt="High Lady of The Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556501727p2/62560505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2597026490?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court?shelf=fantasy-read">fantasy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2597026490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer31943871638038093"><b>
  <i>“For us, the places we went were home. We didn’t care if they were good or evil or neutral or what. We cared about the fact that for the first time, we didn’t have to pretend to be something we weren’t. We just got to be. That made all the difference in the world.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>It seems I’ve found a pattern. Every book that has magic that we all inevitably fall in love with isn’t explained in it’s magnanimity, by its origin, stories that are so improbable even fantasy seems to look at them, wide-eyed and </span>
  <span id="freeText31943871638038093" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“For us, the places we went were home. We didn’t care if they were good or evil or neutral or what. We cared about the fact that for the first time, we didn’t have to pretend to be something we weren’t. We just got to be. That made all the difference in the world.”</i>
</b><br /><br />It seems I’ve found a pattern. Every book that has magic that we all inevitably fall in love with isn’t explained in it’s magnanimity, by its origin, stories that are so improbable even fantasy seems to look at them, wide-eyed and intrigued, the characters that are so unique in ways that make them something so far beyond human and yet struggling to find a place that they can call home. I believe you recognise what I’m trying to say in you own ways, The Night Circus by Erin Morgenstern, Furthermore by Tahereh Mafi, The Hazel Wood by Melissa Albert, and so many more, all books which are nearly entire genres in their own right.<br />And This book is definitely one of them.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“We all have our own ways of trying to go home,” </b>
</i><br /><br />If you’ve read my reviews for some of these books, you’ll notice a pattern and that is because there are a vast amount of things about these books that I love but there are only a few which I can put into words, especially when I’m trapped in that fictional high just after finishing them.<br />There are always a few key points which make these books so phenomenal. The author’s skill at narrating the story in a way that we can grasp while still making the portrayal of the characters and places and simple the magic in the story otherworldly in way which is unique to each of these books is incomprehensible. <br />The fact that I can visualise every world that the author has described, smell the air, feel my heartbeat slow down or speed up is majestical, especially because the world described in this book are not ones you will find anywhere else. Yes, the book draws on the concept of children disappearing into world, which is a tale as old as old as time, but the way that concept has evolved in the rendition of this story is extraordinary. The worlds are not just mysterious or beautiful or magical they are also horrifying, devastating, and deadly.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>”You are the guardians of the secrets of the universe, beloved of worlds that most will never dream of, much less see … can’t you see where you owe it to yourselves to be kind?” </b>
</i><br /><br />It is commonplace to write a story where a child visits a wonderful place and wants nothing but to go back or one where the world is horrible and is traumatised forever, but writing a story where some children have been to places which are frightening and nauseating but have found that they belong there is ingenious. The depiction of character is one of the best parts of this book. You can clearly see that some of these children must have to be so twisted to have thrived in these worlds and some very stereotypically entitled and whiny, and yet when seen through the eyes Seanan Mcguire, the reader clearly sees all the different facets of each child’s personality that tells us that being unusual does not have to mean being depraved.<br /><br />A lot of stereotypes were broken in this book, and I will leave it to you to find out more after reading it. The worlds are enticing, the writing dexterous, and the characters perfect because of their quirks. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Jack and Jill went up the hill, to watch a bit of slaughter, Jack fell down and broke her crown, and Jill came tumbling after.” </b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="31943871638038093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3554709586" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3554709586" />
    <a title="Kevin Kuhn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59568642-kevin-kuhn"><img alt="Kevin Kuhn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508679965p2/59568642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3554709586?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin Kuhn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin Kuhn" href="/user/show/59568642-kevin-kuhn">Kevin Kuhn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59568642-kevin-kuhn?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3554709586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15491283462426562880">What happened to kids like Alice and Dorothy when they returned from their adventures in Wonderland and Oz? They go to Eleanor West’s Home for Wayward Children with dozens of other fantasy land child exiles. <br/><br/>“We don’t teach you how to forget. We teach you how to move on.”<br/><br/>I was lucky enough to have an innocence childhood where the grit and wickedness of the world was revealed slowly. Not all children have that luxury. On the surface, “Every Heart a Doorway” is about the very entertaining concept </span>
  <span id="freeText15491283462426562880" style="display:none">What happened to kids like Alice and Dorothy when they returned from their adventures in Wonderland and Oz? They go to Eleanor West’s Home for Wayward Children with dozens of other fantasy land child exiles. <br /><br />“We don’t teach you how to forget. We teach you how to move on.”<br /><br />I was lucky enough to have an innocence childhood where the grit and wickedness of the world was revealed slowly. Not all children have that luxury. On the surface, “Every Heart a Doorway” is about the very entertaining concept of a home where children who have been whisked away to fantasy lands only to be cast out to reality, are able to guided back into a normal life, surrounded by other children who have had similar adventures. But underneath, I felt like this was about the children who’ve had to face dark realities before they were ready, whether that was abuse, tragedy, or social cruelty. Maybe a reality so cruel they create a fantasy world to escape into. Once you’ve survived that experience, how do you move on? How does your family deal with you?<br /><br />“Their love wanted to fix her, and refused to see that she wasn’t broken.”<br /><br />This book won the 2017 Hugo and Locus for Best Novella. It also won the 2016 Nebula for Best Novella. It’s short and the prose is straightforward, but Author Seanan McGuire slips in little flourishes at just the right time. For such a short work, McGuire takes on a great deal. There are undertones of abuse and the challenge of self-acceptance of gender change and asexuality. <br /><br />“We notice the silence of men. We depend upon the silence of women.”<br /><br />The story gets dark about halfway as McGuire ups the stakes and moves away from a simple teen angst into a harsher tale with life and death consequences. We rush to a no-nonsense finish that wraps up the primary mystery but leaves plenty of offshoots for the inevitable series. <br /><br />My favorite aspect of this is the “meta-ness” of it. The concept of these children who “fall thru a mirror/rabbit hole/doorway,” coming together to make sense of their lives is the best part of the story. But along the way, McGuire finds some wonderful insights and truths that I’m sure hit home with many who have dealt with bleak realities in their youth.<br /><br />"You're nobody's doorway but your own, and the only one who gets to tell you how your story ends is you."<br /><br />A taut story, smartly written about what comes after the escape to fantasy realms and how one decides what is ‘home.’</span>
  <a data-text-id="15491283462426562880" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2150142931" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2150142931" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2150142931?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780765383877" href="/book/show/25667166-every-heart-a-doorway">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Portal fantasy fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2150142931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2467235078890400515"><b>A good enchanting short tale on acceptance and misfits.</b><br/><br/>Hogwarts, Narnia, Middle-Earth, every reader who has tasted speculative fiction will most likely have imagined themselves transported to one, Every Heart A Doorway (EHAD) showed the aftermath of going into these different worlds with no option of going back to them. It’s a great premise and I love how the book told the character’s struggle in coping with their new reality; where even their own family doesn’t trust the things that they experi</span>
  <span id="freeText2467235078890400515" style="display:none"><b>A good enchanting short tale on acceptance and misfits.</b><br><br>Hogwarts, Narnia, Middle-Earth, every reader who has tasted speculative fiction will most likely have imagined themselves transported to one, Every Heart A Doorway (EHAD) showed the aftermath of going into these different worlds with no option of going back to them. It’s a great premise and I love how the book told the character’s struggle in coping with their new reality; where even their own family doesn’t trust the things that they experienced in these worlds. <br><br><b>Picture: Official Artworks by Rovina Cai</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508600422i/24233564._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508600422i/24233565._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“This world is unforgiving and cruel to those it judges as even the slightest bit outside the norm.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br> <br>For such a short book—around 2 hours read—EHAD managed to talk about a lot of important topics regarding diversity, bullying and most importantly, acceptance; not to mention McGuire’s prose is so damn lovely and enchanting to read. There are so many phrases that I highlighted just from the first part of the book.<br><br>This is a good novella, but in my opinion, without a doubt highly overrated. This book is divided into two parts and let me tell you, the first part of this book is amazing, at this point I honestly thought it would be 5 stars read, which would also make this book automatically be the first YA book I’ve rated 5 stars. However, the second part of the book disappointed me, my interest dwindled as the story turns into a murder mystery and I can’t help but feel that McGuire tried to put too many things to discuss within this short story; at the same time, this made the character's personality fell flat to me as well.<br><br>EHAD is a good short story but from the first book alone, I still don’t know whether I’ll continue with this series up until the end or not yet, especially after knowing there will be at least six books in it. However, I will read the second book before making my final decision. I recommend this to anyone who’s looking for a good short portal fantasy read. This book received tons of awards, quite highly praised among YA community, there’s a high chance you’re going to enjoy this much more than me.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“You’re nobody’s doorway but your own, and the only one who gets to tell you how your story ends is you.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><i>This review can also be found on my dear friend, Haifa's blog: <a href="https://booksprens.com/2017/10/22/every-heart-a-doorway-wayward-children-1-by-senan-mcguire/comment-page-1/#comment-295/" rel="nofollow noopener">Booksprens</a></i><br><br><i>You can find the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <b><a href="http://booknest.eu/review/patrick" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></b></i></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer518939367415209343">*4.5/5 stars<br/><br/><i>We notice the silence of men. We depend upon the silence of women.</i><br/><br/>This book was heart-achingly beautiful. I don't even know how to coherently arrange my thoughts to explain the way this book dragged me in from beginning to end. I adore compact narratives. And it handled it beautifully. It was odd, m</span>
  <span id="freeText518939367415209343" style="display:none">*4.5/5 stars<br /><br /><i>We notice the silence of men. We depend upon the silence of women.</i><br /><br />This book was heart-achingly beautiful. I don't even know how to coherently arrange my thoughts to explain the way this book dragged me in from beginning to end. I adore compact narratives. I think they have the potential to say so much in so few words, and this has definitely fallen among my favorite books that say so much in such little space. This book was about identity. And it handled it beautifully. It was odd, melancholy, and captivating. Not to mention the inclusion of an asexual main character whose identity is confirmed on the page and actually discussed. As well as a side character who is a trans boy and whose identity is also discussed in such a fascinating and wonderful way. An incredible story overall. </span>

<div id="review_2306558212" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2306558212" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2306558212?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2306558212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14658057677844033390"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>You’re nobody’s doorway but your own, and the only one who gets to tell you how your story ends is you.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br/><br/>It seems like I have <i>finally</i> stumbled upon the lives of the Wayward children. <br/><br/><b>The book is underrated as in not many people have read it, but its overrated as in it gets too much hype.</b> My expectations were so high, I was really hoping to binge read the whole trilogy that's out and fall in love with the author's writing, characters, and the whole idea of the story. I ended up checkin</span>
  <span id="freeText14658057677844033390" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>You’re nobody’s doorway but your own, and the only one who gets to tell you how your story ends is you.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br /><br />It seems like I have <i>finally</i> stumbled upon the lives of the Wayward children. <br /><br /><b>The book is underrated as in not many people have read it, but its overrated as in it gets too much hype.</b> My expectations were so high, I was really hoping to binge read the whole trilogy that's out and fall in love with the author's writing, characters, and the whole idea of the story. I ended up checking the whole trilogy from my library because I wanted to read them without having doubts and enjoy the full ride. This is why I hate having high expectations (or any sort of expectations) for a book. Truthfully, I feel like it was too short for what it offered, for what it gave. I feel like McGuire wanted to make the story short so she added everything together, not adding enough or adding too much.<br /><br />The whole idea seemed enchanting to me. When I first started reading <i>Every Heart a Doorway</i>, it felt like I was also taken to a school where no one accepted what I saw except for the rest of the students. It was as if I was in this world and the world the students here traveled, such as Narnia, The Goblin Market, Alice in Wonderland, etc. But in the end, I was not in any story but my own one, and it was sad. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Eleanor West spent her days giving them what she had never had and hoped that someday, it would be enough to pay her passage back to the place where she belonged.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><i>Every Heart a Doorway</i> is the story we all wish we can fall into. Students have fallen or been thrown into a magical land which they now call home. Fairyland, Candyland, The Gobling Market, these are places students have explored and fallen in love with that they cannot go back. Parents send their children to a boarding school created by Eleanor West, the only one who understands and knows what its like to experience a land filled with creations and things others wouldn't understand. <br /><br /><b>Filled with trauma, nostalgia, acceptance, and betrayal, the magical story of how these kids are coping with their dreams suddenly turned into reality begins.</b><br /><br />I had seen so many good and positive reviews about this series that I knew I had to read it someday, especially before the 4th and 5th book come out. I loved the idea of it, but it turned out that I wanted nothing more than to finish it just to be over with it because I was so...bored. The first star is given because the writing is beautifully persuasive and the representation held is something else I have been wanting to read about. The representation of having an ace and trans character holds a special place in the book. Seanan McGuire was able to make Nancy explain the difference between asexual and aromantic in a way that many people can find resourceful to understand the differences. It can even be useful to understand what asexuality itself means, although Nancy doesn't mention it much, only once or twice (unless I missed the other time(s)). Not to mention, <b>the atmosphere in this is beautiful</b>. Seanan really describes the atmosphere and world beautiful so pleasurably aesthetic and you can’t do anything but imagine it all. It’s beautifully crafted and I truly wish it was true, the idea of going to a land where you consider home because your real home is nothing but a place that exists. <br /><br />The other reason I'm giving it 2 stars is because I really and genuinely adored Kade's character. The way he handled his gender identity, reason, and bullying was what made me fall for him. He had been called a girl before because of who he was and took the insult of it calmly, not seeming to care and instead wanting to not even bother arguing because he seemed like he didn't care. He was happy where he was and he knew who he was, and his own love and acceptance was all that mattered to him and I loved that. I loved that he grew to love his identity, himself and accept the fact that there will be people who won't love you because you transitioned from a girl to a boy. I really hope McGuire decides to write a book about his characters and the land he traveled to and how he came to transitioning to a boy, a prince. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>We don't teach you how to dwell. We also don't teach you how to forget. We teach you how to move on.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The rest of the characters felt dull and flat to me. There was nothing to love about anyone. From Nancy to Sumi, Christopher, Jack, Jill, and everyone else, I felt like no one had a story besides Kade. Even Ms. Eleanor had a story but it was not told. The book is very short that not enough information about anyone was given. We're told the lands they travel to, what happened before and after, but other than that, no background information is given on either. The most we got was from Jack and Jill, but its fine because <i>Down Among the Sticks and Bones</i>, is about them, and to be honest, I'm quite excited about it. Although it doesn't mention it, Jack, to me, seemed liked she was part of the LGBTQ+ community. I'm not sure what her orientation was (or would be), but she was different than all the other girls. She was weird and strange, odd and mean, caring yet heartless. <br /><br />Adding to that, I wouldn't call this a mystery. I was excited that it was, but I don't think it would fit the category/bookshelf. It's very easy to find out who the "mystery" is because of how it happens. The character describes themselves in a way no one else does and you can't help but think that they're the "mysterious" one. <br /><br />There isn't much more to say because there isn't much to take from. The beginning was fine, there is not middle, and the ending felt rushed. I do think Seanan wanted to make the book short so she rushed everything, concluding everything, and not adding a middle. If there was a middle, another 80 pages or so would be added. I'm not asking for info-dump, but we lack information.<br /><br />I also just found out Seanan McGuire is Mira Grant and I've been wanting to read her book <i>Into the Rolling Deep</i> for so long now so hopefully that one will make up for this one. They're the same but the fictional worlds are completely different. She's a lot darker as Mira Grant and although EHaD is dark, it is more like creaturely-dark and weird. The vibe you get when reading this is beautiful because of her worldbuilding and how you can't help but imagine every land described. The smells, the sights, the creatures, the creations--every little detail is imaginably beautiful.<br /><br />This is why, folks, we should never rely on reviews and ratings all the time. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Hope means you keep on holding to things that won't ever be so again, and so you bleed an inch at a time until there's nothing left.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="14658057677844033390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1937955681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer887680445218907356"><blockquote>
  <i>Their love wanted to fix her, and refused to see that she wasn't broken.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>I think I might have needed to adjust my expectations from novel-goals to novella-goals.</b> I judged this as a book. I did not judge this as a novella. To be fair, I do think this novella could've done with more character work and that all-important middle section. But the fact remains that <b>my rating and review of this is slightly unfair,</b> and I've definitely enjoyed later works <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1937956085' rel='nofollow noopener'>Down Among the Sticks and Bones</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1996572927' rel='nofollow noopener'>Beneath th</a></span>
  <span id="freeText887680445218907356" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Their love wanted to fix her, and refused to see that she wasn't broken.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>I think I might have needed to adjust my expectations from novel-goals to novella-goals.</b> I judged this as a book. I did not judge this as a novella. To be fair, I do think this novella could've done with more character work and that all-important middle section. But the fact remains that <b>my rating and review of this is slightly unfair,</b> and I've definitely enjoyed later works <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1937956085" rel="nofollow noopener">Down Among the Sticks and Bones</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1996572927" rel="nofollow noopener">Beneath the Sugar Sky</a> far more than I did this. This book especially, however, <b>lacks a middle.</b><br /><br /><br /><b>// POSITIVES</b><br /><br />So many books have talked about the secret doorway into the unknown, the passage through an unknown door. <i>Every Heart A Doorway</i> is about what happens to those kids when they come back to the “real world”. Sounds like an <b>awesome concept</b>? It totally is. And to some degree, I think it's executed well. <br /><br /><b>Seanan Mcguire’s language is gorgeous</b>. Her dialogue is snappy and fun, but the narrative language is beautiful - the perfect balance. <blockquote>
  <i>“Hope is a knife that can cut through the foundations of the world... Hope hurts. That's what you need to learn, and fast, if you don't want it to cut you open from the inside out.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />This book does nail diversity. There’s an ace main character and a trans side character, which was <i>awesome</i>. The ace character was definitely represented well; I especially liked that the book separated asexuality and aromanticism, because oh dang, some people do not seem to understand they're different. I did think the initial description seemed almost... cheesy? It's good rep, I just thought the page on which Nancy <i>explains</i> asexuality was written a little clunkily. She spends around a page thinking about it, probably as a way to educate readers who don't know what asexuality is; I suppose I just found it too "now I'm explaining things" infodumpy. <br /><br />I did also like that all the diversity was incidental, while not being tokenistic. This is a hard balance to get right, but I thought it was done perfectly. Not a single character is defined by being lgbt, but it's ALSO not simply thrown in with. I think I missed something because I didn’t notice the existence of a gay character and I keep seeing reviews mentioning her. Was it Jack or is that my wishful lesbian brain?<br /><br />There's some interesting thematic work around PSTD and mental illness, which was nice. I also <i>loved</i> the subtle feminism woven throughout the book. <blockquote>
  <i>Because ‘boys will be boys’ is a self-fulfilling prophecy,” said Lundy. “They’re too loud, on the whole, to be easily misplaced or overlooked; when they disappear from the home, parents send search parties to dredge them out of swamps and drag them away from frog ponds. It’s not innate. It’s learned. But it protects them from the doors, keeps them safe at home. Call it irony, if you like, but we spend so much time waiting for our boys to stray that they never have the opportunity. We notice the silence of men. We depend upon the silence of women.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The characters here are fleshed-out and interesting. I was a big fan of Jack, who’s morally ambiguous and funny. <blockquote>
  <i><br />Corpses are incapable of offering informed consent, and are hence no better than vibrators.</i>
</blockquote><br />And of course, there's the <b>witty, entertaining dialogue</b>. <br /><br /><br /><b>// NEGATIVES</b><br /><br />Nancy, unfortunately, didn’t leave much of a mark on me. She’s not a bad character; she never annoyed me. But <b>she didn’t have a character arc</b>. <i>Why</i> did she not have a character arc? Because <i>Every Heart A Doorway</i> was not nearly long enough (shocking, right?), and therein lies my main problem with this book; <b>this book is just not fleshed out enough.</b> <br /><br /><i>Every Heart A Doorway</i> is the first 100 pages and the last 70 pages of an incredible book. It feels like there was something missing. I felt the need to try and frame this book with the three-act structure, but I couldn’t, because there is literally no middle section. In general, the book feels rushed and underdone. Which <i>sucks</i>, because with a middle section added, this could have been one of the best books ever written. <br /><br />VERDICT: This book needed more of a middle, but I'd still recommend this as a <i>series</i> for the scope of the story. <br /><br /><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/girladamparrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="887680445218907356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

I'm also Mira Grant (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.miragrant.com'>www.miragrant.com</a>), author of <i>Feed</i> and <i>Deadline</i>.<br/><br/>Born and raised in Northern California, I fear weather and am remarkably laid-back about rattlesnakes. I watch too many horror movies, read too many comic books, and </span>
  <span id="freeText6205367983662354993" style="display:none">Hi! I'm Seanan McGuire, author of the Toby Daye series (<i>Rosemary and Rue</i>, <i>A Local Habitation</i>, <i>An Artificial Night</i>, <i>Late Eclipses</i>), as well as a lot of other things. I'm also Mira Grant (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.miragrant.com">www.miragrant.com</a>), author of <i>Feed</i> and <i>Deadline</i>.<br /><br />Born and raised in Northern California, I fear weather and am remarkably laid-back about rattlesnakes. I watch too many horror movies, read too many comic books, and share my house with two monsters in feline form, Lilly and Alice (Siamese and Maine Coon).<br /><br />I <i>do not</i> check this inbox. Please don't send me messages through Goodreads; they won't be answered. I don't want to have to delete this account. :(</span>
